<!-- .slide: data-bg-epic -->

# So you want to change Ember?

---

> You can do this! 
<!-- .element: class="zoey"-->

Note: 
Zoey is here to help us along, just like in the Guides!
And what better way to start to this adventure then getting to know your fellow adventurers

---

## Introduce yourself

- How long have you been working with Ember? 
- What do you know about the RFC process?
- What makes it easier or harder for you to contribute to Ember.JS?

Note:
Please pick a neighbour, next to you or front/back that you are the least familiar with. We are also here for the community part :) and use these questions as prompts. You have 2 minutes, so make sure both of you share something.

I hope you had a nice intro, the second question mentioned RFC.

---

<!-- .slide: data-bg-epic -->
## The Request For Comments Process

Note: 
The RFC stands for request for comments, the process we use within Ember to make changes to the framework and everything that is under the perview of the core-teams. 

---

<!-- .slide: data-bg-epic -->
## The RFC process

Note:
We use the RFC process for short. I always read it as a request for a change.

---

<!-- .slide: data-auto-animate -->

### When?

---

<!-- .slide: data-auto-animate -->

### When?
> Time for a quiz 
<!-- .element: class="zoey"-->

---

<!-- .slide: data-bg-green -->
1. <!-- .element: class="fragment"-->
  Introducing `.gjs`
2. Adding a warning to an endpoint <!-- .element: class="fragment"-->
3. Built-in template whitespace minification <!-- .element: class="fragment"-->
4. Adding browser support for Arch <!-- .element: class="fragment"-->

Note:
 # RFC Required
  - New feature that adds API surface area
  - Feature removals from a release channel
  - New idiomatic usage or conventions
     
  # No RFC Needed
  - Rephrasing, reorganizing, or refactoring
  - Addition or removal of warnings
  - Improvements to objective quality metrics (e.g., speed)
  - Changes only noticed by Ember implementors

  1. RFC number is Sevenhunderd and seventy nine 779
  3. Started as making an addon default in Ember, 1121
  4. So eventhough some documentation might say this as green, adding a browser adds maintaince for core teams, changing our testing strategy and deciding on how to keep supporting this in the future, so this does require an RFC

---

> I have an idea, please comment on it!
<!-- .element: class="null-vox"-->

---

> Just follow the template! 
<!-- .element: class="zoey"-->

---

### Template

- Title
- Summary
- Why?
- How?
- Why not/alternatives

Note:
RFC 617 was the first RFC to go through all these stages, because it was also the RFC that introduced them. So let's figure out what these stages are about.
- **Proposed** 
  **Interaction:** Red/Green — “When you’ve filled in the template and created a PR, is your RFC now Proposed?”
  Someone has written the idea down in the RFC repo and create a PR — it’s on the table for discussion.  
  You can go to the EmberJS Discord and there is the #dev-rfc where you can ask people for input on your RFC, or even before filling in the template and making the PR discuss with others.

- **Exploring** 
  The relevant core team(s) decide it's worth continueing to discuss, the community starts working out the details, questions, and trade-offs. This is the time to basically figure out our list of requirements, not just by the core team, but by all of us. From this point forward a RFC has a champion, which is a person that represents the core team and will help shepperd the RFC through all it’s stages  
  
  Before this RFC moves to the next stage it needs to go through a Final Comment Period. This concept is basically a week in which, we the community can say, but you forgot about this. If it would be a wedding this is the point to “speak up now or forever hold your silence”. Not completely true, because you can always make a new RFC to revert this decision, but that should not happen often. Every friday at 20:00 in this timezone there is a RFC meeting in our discord server. This is basically a project management meeting to see where RFCs are at and what needs to happen. If they are matching the criteria for the next phase the FCP will start.
  **Interaction:** Red/Green — “Could an RFC skip Exploring?”


- **Accepted**  
  Completing the FCP, the RFC is now accepter. The RFC has a clear direction, requirements and community agreement that it’s a good idea.
  **Interaction:** Open floor — “So what needs to happen now it’s moved to Accepted?”
  We, the community and the core teams will start building/implementing the things described in the RFC

  Sometimes we decide to not move forward because the RFC does not work. _TODO add something about paradigm shifts/tech stuff improving with time_. If the RFC is in the proposed or exploring stage it will be closed, when it's stopped after being accepted we call it discontinued.

  Queue another FCP, it’s time to make sure we’ve met our criteria.

- **Ready for Release**  
  The implementation is done and lined up to ship in an Ember release.
  **Interaction:** Open floor — “What do we do to make this transition happen?”

- **Released**  
  The feature is in the framework — you can already use it in your app.  

- **Recommended** 
  So if we consider the feature a finished kitchen, the next stage is hosting a dinner party. Recommended means as much as sharing it with your friends and family to see that it works. We have another FCP to make sure there is concensus about hosting this dinner party! Because we need to make sure that:
  - Addopted througout the learning materials
  - Adpoted by addons etc

###### rfcs.emberjs.com


Note: 
- You have 5 minutes to locate  
  - a RFC that could use your input to figure out where it's going
  - a RFC that could use some of your coding capacity to move forward
  - a RFC that is missing a champion
  - find information about the RFC process that was unclear up till now
  - anything else you want to find :)

- Red/Green: Did you find what you were looking for?

Note: 
1. Before today: Were you already confident contributing to RFCs?
   - Green = yes, Red = no

2. After today: Did your confidence increase?
   - Green = yes, Red = no

If you were Red → Green, that is exactly the goal of today.
If you’re Green → Red or Red → Red, thank you for the honest signal—come grab me or ping #dev-ember-learning so we can unblock what's unclear.”
